<p><b>Lincolnshire</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ŋ/: 'ng' in 'sing'">ŋ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ən/: 'on' in 'button'">ən</span><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ər/: 'er' in 'letter'">ər</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ɪər/: 'ear' in 'near'">ɪər</span></span>/</a></span></span>; abbreviated <b>Lincs</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_England" title="Counties of England">county</a> in the east of <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>. It borders <a href="/wiki/Norfolk" title="Norfolk">Norfolk</a> to the south east, <a href="/wiki/Cambridgeshire" title="Cambridgeshire">Cambridgeshire</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Rutland" title="Rutland">Rutland</a> to the south west, <a href="/wiki/Leicestershire" title="Leicestershire">Leicestershire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nottinghamshire" title="Nottinghamshire">Nottinghamshire</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/South_Yorkshire" title="South Yorkshire">South Yorkshire</a> to the northwest, and the <a href="/wiki/East_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="East Riding of Yorkshire">East Riding of Yorkshire</a> to the north. It also borders <a href="/wiki/Northamptonshire" title="Northamptonshire">Northamptonshire</a> in the south for just 20 yards (18&#160;m), England's shortest county boundary.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/County_town" title="County town">county town</a> is <a href="/wiki/Lincoln,_England" title="Lincoln, England">Lincoln</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/County_council" title="County council">county council</a> has its headquarters.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_counties_of_England" title="Ceremonial counties of England">ceremonial county</a> of Lincolnshire is composed of the <a href="/wiki/Non-metropolitan_county" title="Non-metropolitan county">non-metropolitan county</a> of Lincolnshire and the area covered by the <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authorities</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_Lincolnshire" title="North Lincolnshire">North Lincolnshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_East_Lincolnshire" title="North East Lincolnshire">North East Lincolnshire</a>. Therefore, part of the ceremonial county is in the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_and_the_Humber" title="Yorkshire and the Humber">Yorkshire and the Humber</a> <a href="/wiki/Region_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Region of England">region of England</a>, and most is in the <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands" title="East Midlands">East Midlands</a> region. The county is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_ceremonial_counties_of_England" title="List of ceremonial counties of England">second-largest of the English ceremonial counties</a> and one that is predominantly agricultural in land use. The county is fourth largest of the two-tier counties, as the unitary authorities of North Lincolnshire and North East Lincolnshire are not included. The county can be broken down into a number of geographical sub-regions including: The rolling chalk hills of the <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_Wolds" title="Lincolnshire Wolds">Lincolnshire Wolds</a>. In the south east are the <a href="/wiki/The_Fens" title="The Fens">Lincolnshire Fens</a> (south-east Lincolnshire), the Carrs (similar to the Fens but in north Lincolnshire), the industrial <a href="/wiki/Humber" title="Humber">Humber Estuary</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> coast around <a href="/wiki/Grimsby" title="Grimsby">Grimsby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe" title="Scunthorpe">Scunthorpe</a>, and in the south-west of the county, the Kesteven Uplands, comprising rolling limestone hills in the district of <a href="/wiki/South_Kesteven" title="South Kesteven">South Kesteven</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Lincolnshire" title="History of Lincolnshire">History of Lincolnshire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincoln_-_Castle_Square.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Lincoln_-_Castle_Square.jpg/220px-Lincoln_-_Castle_Square.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Lincoln_-_Castle_Square.jpg/330px-Lincoln_-_Castle_Square.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Lincoln_-_Castle_Square.jpg/440px-Lincoln_-_Castle_Square.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincoln_-_Castle_Square.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Part of 'The Bailgate'. The centre of the uphill area of Lincoln.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Lincolnshire derived from the merging of the territory of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Lindsey" title="Kingdom of Lindsey">Kingdom of Lindsey</a> with that controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Danelaw" title="Danelaw">Danelaw</a> <a href="/wiki/Borough" title="Borough">borough</a> of <a href="/wiki/Stamford,_Lincolnshire" title="Stamford, Lincolnshire">Stamford</a>. For some time the entire county was called "Lindsey", and it is recorded as such in the 11th-century <i><a href="/wiki/Domesday_Book" title="Domesday Book">Domesday Book</a>.</i> Later, the name <a href="/wiki/Lindsey_(government_district)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lindsey (government district)">Lindsey</a> was applied to the northern core, around Lincoln, and this emerged as one of the three <a href="/wiki/Parts_of_Lincolnshire" title="Parts of Lincolnshire">Parts of Lincolnshire</a>, along with the Parts of <a href="/wiki/Holland,_Lincolnshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Holland, Lincolnshire">Holland</a> in the south-east and the Parts of <a href="/wiki/Kesteven" title="Kesteven">Kesteven</a> in the south-west, which each had separate <a href="/wiki/Quarter_Sessions" class="mw-redirect" title="Quarter Sessions">Quarter Sessions</a> as their county administrations.</p>
<p>In 1888 when <a href="/wiki/County_council" title="County council">county councils</a> were set up, Lindsey, Holland and Kesteven each received separate ones. These survived until 1974, when Holland, Kesteven, and most of Lindsey were unified into Lincolnshire. The northern part of Lindsey, including <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe" title="Scunthorpe">Scunthorpe</a> Municipal Borough and <a href="/wiki/Grimsby" title="Grimsby">Grimsby</a> County Borough, was incorporated into the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Shire_county" class="mw-redirect" title="Shire county">non-metropolitan county</a> of <a href="/wiki/Humberside" title="Humberside">Humberside</a>, along with most of the <a href="/wiki/East_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="East Riding of Yorkshire">East Riding of Yorkshire</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincolnshire_Admin_Counties_1890-1965.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Lincolnshire_Admin_Counties_1890-1965.png/220px-Lincolnshire_Admin_Counties_1890-1965.png" width="220" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Lincolnshire_Admin_Counties_1890-1965.png/330px-Lincolnshire_Admin_Counties_1890-1965.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Lincolnshire_Admin_Counties_1890-1965.png/440px-Lincolnshire_Admin_Counties_1890-1965.png 2x" data-file-width="453" data-file-height="621" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincolnshire_Admin_Counties_1890-1965.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
County and County Borough areas pre 1965</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A local government reform in 1996 abolished Humberside, and the land south of the Humber was allocated to the <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authorities" class="mw-redirect" title="Unitary authorities">unitary authorities</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_Lincolnshire" title="North Lincolnshire">North Lincolnshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_East_Lincolnshire" title="North East Lincolnshire">North East Lincolnshire</a>. These two areas became part of Lincolnshire for ceremonial purposes such as the <a href="/wiki/Lord-Lieutenant" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord-Lieutenant">Lord-Lieutenancy</a>, but are not covered by the Lincolnshire police and are in the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_and_the_Humber" title="Yorkshire and the Humber">Yorkshire and the Humber</a> region.</p>
<p>The remaining districts of Lincolnshire are <a href="/wiki/Boston_(borough)" class="mw-redirect" title="Boston (borough)">Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Lindsey" title="East Lindsey">East Lindsey</a>, Lincoln, <a href="/wiki/North_Kesteven" title="North Kesteven">North Kesteven</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Holland,_England" class="mw-redirect" title="South Holland, England">South Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Kesteven" title="South Kesteven">South Kesteven</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Lindsey" title="West Lindsey">West Lindsey</a>. They are part of the <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands" title="East Midlands">East Midlands</a> region.</p>
<p>The area was shaken by the 27 February <a href="/wiki/2008_Lincolnshire_earthquake" title="2008 Lincolnshire earthquake">2008 Lincolnshire earthquake</a>, reaching between 4.7 and 5.3 on the <a href="/wiki/Richter_magnitude_scale" title="Richter magnitude scale">Richter magnitude scale</a>; it was one of the largest earthquakes to affect Britain in recent years.</p>
<p>Lincolnshire is home to <a href="/wiki/Woolsthorpe_Manor" title="Woolsthorpe Manor">Woolsthorpe Manor</a>, birthplace and home of Sir <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Isaac Newton</a>. He attended <a href="/wiki/The_King%27s_School,_Grantham" title="The King's School, Grantham">The King's School, Grantham</a> and its library has preserved his signature, applied to a window sill when he was a teenager.</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lincolnshire's geography is fairly varied, but consists of several distinct areas:</p>
<ul>
<li>Lincolnshire Wolds - area of rolling hills in the North East of the county designated an Area of Outstanding Natural Beauty</li>
<li>The Fens - dominating the South East quarter of the county</li>
<li>The Marshes - running along the coast of the county</li>
<li>The Lincoln Edge/Cliff - limestone escarpment running north-south along the Western half of the county</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This is a chart of trend of regional <a href="/wiki/Gross_value_added" title="Gross value added">gross value added</a> of Lincolnshire at current basic prices <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://webarchive.nationalarchives.gov.uk/20050303060209/http://www.statistics.gov.uk/downloads/theme_economy/RegionalGVA.pdf">published</a> (pp.&#160;240–253) by <i>Office for National Statistics</i> with figures in millions of British Pounds Sterling.</p>

</dl>
<p>Notable businesses based in Lincolnshire include the <a href="/wiki/Lincs_FM_Group" title="Lincs FM Group">Lincs FM Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Young%27s_Seafood" title="Young's Seafood">Young's Seafood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Openfield" title="Openfield">Openfield</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_Co-operative" title="Lincolnshire Co-operative">Lincolnshire Co-operative</a> (whose membership includes about one quarter of the population of the county).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincsfarmland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Lincsfarmland.jpg/220px-Lincsfarmland.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Lincsfarmland.jpg/330px-Lincsfarmland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Lincsfarmland.jpg/440px-Lincsfarmland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincsfarmland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lincolnshire farmland near <a href="/wiki/Burton_Coggles" title="Burton Coggles">Burton Coggles</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Lincolnshire is an agricultural area, growing large amounts of wheat, <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugar_beet" title="Sugar beet">sugar beet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oilseed_rape" class="mw-redirect" title="Oilseed rape">oilseed rape</a>. In South Lincolnshire, where the soil is particularly rich in nutrients, some of the most common crops include potatoes, <a href="/wiki/Cabbage" title="Cabbage">cabbages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cauliflower" title="Cauliflower">cauliflowers</a>, and onions. South Lincolnshire is also home to one of the UK's leading <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_experiment_station" title="Agricultural experiment station">agricultural experiment stations</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Sutton_Bridge" title="Sutton Bridge">Sutton Bridge</a> operated by the <a href="/wiki/Potato_Council" title="Potato Council">Potato Council</a>, Sutton Bridge Crop Storage Research engages in research for the British potato industry.<sup id="cite_ref-PCSB_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCSB-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mechanisation around 1900 greatly diminished the number of workers required to operate the county's relatively large farms, and the proportion of workers in the agricultural sector dropped substantially during this period. Several major engineering companies developed in Lincoln, <a href="/wiki/Gainsborough,_Lincolnshire" title="Gainsborough, Lincolnshire">Gainsborough</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grantham" title="Grantham">Grantham</a> to support those changes, perhaps most famously <a href="/wiki/William_Foster_%26_Co_Ltd" class="mw-redirect" title="William Foster &amp; Co Ltd">Fosters of Lincoln</a>, who built the first <a href="/wiki/Tank" title="Tank">tank</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Hornsby_%26_Sons" title="Richard Hornsby &amp; Sons">Richard Hornsby &amp; Sons</a> of Grantham. Most such companies are long gone, and Lincolnshire is no longer an engineering centre.</p>
<p>Today, immigrant workers mainly from <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">new member states of the European Union</a> in Central and Eastern Europe comprise a large component of the seasonal agricultural workforce, particularly in the south of the county where more labour-intensive crops such as small vegetables and cut flowers are typically grown. This seasonal influx of migrant labour occasionally causes tension between the migrant workforce and local people, in a county which is relatively unaccustomed to large-scale immigration. However, as a result of the current economic climate some food production facilities have closed down, this has caused some reduction in the levels of migrant workers. The large number of people from <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> is still obvious in the town of Boston, and in Grantham the number of <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Polish</a> workers is apparent.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

</div>
</div>
<p>The Conservative Party won nine seats in the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Kingdom_general_election" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 United Kingdom general election">2010 United Kingdom general election</a> in Lincolnshire, considerably increasing their vote share at the expense of Labour, taking <a href="/wiki/Gillian_Merron" title="Gillian Merron">Gillian Merron</a>'s Lincoln constituency.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lincolnshire_County_Council">Lincolnshire County Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Lincolnshire County Council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincolnshire_County_Council_election,_2017.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Lincolnshire_County_Council_election%2C_2017.svg/220px-Lincolnshire_County_Council_election%2C_2017.svg.png" width="220" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Lincolnshire_County_Council_election%2C_2017.svg/330px-Lincolnshire_County_Council_election%2C_2017.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Lincolnshire_County_Council_election%2C_2017.svg/440px-Lincolnshire_County_Council_election%2C_2017.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1086" data-file-height="1305" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincolnshire_County_Council_election,_2017.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of outcome of <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_County_Council_election,_2017" title="Lincolnshire County Council election, 2017">Lincolnshire County Council election, 2017</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_UK" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservative Party UK">Conservatives</a> retook control of the council, winning 58 of the 70 seats. <a href="/wiki/North_Lincolnshire" title="North Lincolnshire">North Lincolnshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_East_Lincolnshire" title="North East Lincolnshire">North East Lincolnshire</a> are <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authorities</a> and do not form part of the <a href="/wiki/Non-metropolitan_county" title="Non-metropolitan county">non-metropolitan county</a> of Lincolnshire</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_UK" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservative Party UK">Conservatives</a> control the county council, with 58 of the 70 seats. <a href="/wiki/North_Lincolnshire" title="North Lincolnshire">North Lincolnshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_East_Lincolnshire" title="North East Lincolnshire">North East Lincolnshire</a> are <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authorities</a> and do not form part of the <a href="/wiki/Non-metropolitan_county" title="Non-metropolitan county">non-metropolitan county</a> of Lincolnshire.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2009_election">2009 election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2009 election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Conservative Party comfortably controlled the County Council after the <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_County_Council_election,_2009" title="Lincolnshire County Council election, 2009">2009 local elections</a>, in which they increased their majority to 43 seats. The Labour Party lost a total of 15 seats including 7 in Lincoln, whilst the Liberal Democrats lost three. The <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_Independents" title="Lincolnshire Independents">Lincolnshire Independents</a> gained a total of four seats, although one of their number moved to the Conservative group during 2010, increasing the number of Conservative seats to 61. The collective group of the Lincolnshire Independents, the Boston Bypass Party and other independent councillors formed the opposition for the four-year term.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_election">2013 election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2013 election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_County_Council_election,_2013" title="Lincolnshire County Council election, 2013">2013 County Council elections</a>, the Conservatives lost their overall majority and formed a coalition with the Liberal Democrats and independents. The <a href="/wiki/UK_Independence_Party" title="UK Independence Party">UK Independence Party</a> made significant gains from the Conservatives, particularly around the town of <a href="/wiki/Boston,_Lincolnshire" title="Boston, Lincolnshire">Boston</a>, due to opposition to Eastern European immigration.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>UKIP were initially the main opposition party with 16 councillors, but six members broke away to form a separate group, UKIP Lincolnshire.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2017_election">2017 election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2017 election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_County_Council_election,_2017" title="Lincolnshire County Council election, 2017">Lincolnshire County Council election, 2017</a> took place on 4 May 2017 and saw a local landslide victory for the Conservatives, who won 58 out of the 70 seats. UKIP was left without a single seat. Labour lost four seats, reducing their number of seats to six, the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> were reduced to one seat, and the <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_Independents" title="Lincolnshire Independents">Lincolnshire Independents</a> were also reduced to a single seat after losing eight seats. Four other independents were elected.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Referendums">Referendums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Referendums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1975_European_Communities_membership">1975 European Communities membership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 1975 European Communities membership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Communities_membership_referendum,_1975" title="United Kingdom European Communities membership referendum, 1975">1975 EC membership referendum</a> was the first major referendum ever to be held within the county, and saw a large majority of voters approve continued membership of the then <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Communities</a> within non-metropolitan Lincolnshire and also <a href="/wiki/Humberside" title="Humberside">Humberside</a>, which included northern parts of historic Lincolnshire. The referendum was held on 5 June 1975 with all the votes counted centrally under the provisions of the <a href="/wiki/Referendum_Act_1975" title="Referendum Act 1975">Referendum Act 1975</a>. The result was declared on the following day.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011_Alternative_Vote">2011 Alternative Vote</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2011 Alternative Vote">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Alternative_Vote_referendum,_2011" title="United Kingdom Alternative Vote referendum, 2011">United Kingdom Alternative Vote referendum, 2011</a> was the first to be held within Lincolnshire since the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Communities_membership_referendum,_1975" title="United Kingdom European Communities membership referendum, 1975">1975 EC membership referendum</a> and was only the second time that the people of Lincolnshire have been asked to vote in a referendum. The referendum asked voters whether to replace the present "<a href="/wiki/Plurality_voting_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Plurality voting system">first-past-the-post</a>" (simple plurality) system with the "<a href="/wiki/Instant-runoff_voting" title="Instant-runoff voting">alternative vote</a>" (AV) method for electing MPs to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a> in future general elections. The proposal to introduce AV was overwhelmingly rejected by voters with all eight counting areas within Lincolnshire returning significant "no" votes.</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:right; font-size:100%;">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016_European_Union_membership">2016 European Union membership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2016 European Union membership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On Thursday 23 June 2016, in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">EU referendum</a>, the people of Lincolnshire voted for the second time on the issue of the UK's continued membership of what is now known as the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> under the provisions of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Referendum_Act_2015" title="European Union Referendum Act 2015">European Union Referendum Act 2015</a>. Of the ten MPs which represented the historic county at the time six MPs <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Percy" title="Andrew Percy">Andrew Percy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Vickers" title="Martin Vickers">Martin Vickers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edward_Leigh" title="Edward Leigh">Edward Leigh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karl_McCartney" title="Karl McCartney">Karl McCartney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nick_Boles" title="Nick Boles">Nick Boles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Phillips_(politician)" title="Stephen Phillips (politician)">Stephen Phillips</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Hayes_(British_politician)" title="John Hayes (British politician)">John Hayes</a> supported a "Leave" vote with four MPs <a href="/wiki/Matt_Warman" title="Matt Warman">Matt Warman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Atkins" title="Victoria Atkins">Victoria Atkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melanie_Onn" title="Melanie Onn">Melanie Onn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nic_Dakin" title="Nic Dakin">Nic Dakin</a> who supported a "Remain" vote.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Police_and_Crime_Commissioners">Police and Crime Commissioners</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Police and Crime Commissioners">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_Police_and_Crime_Commissioner" title="Lincolnshire Police and Crime Commissioner">Lincolnshire Police and Crime Commissioner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humberside_Police_and_Crime_Commissioner" title="Humberside Police and Crime Commissioner">Humberside Police and Crime Commissioner</a></div>
<p>The most recent elections for <a href="/wiki/Police_and_Crime_Commissioner" class="mw-redirect" title="Police and Crime Commissioner">Police and Crime Commissioners</a> within the Lincolnshire and Humberside police force areas took place on Thursday 5 May 2016.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services_and_retail">Services and retail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Services and retail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to an IGGI<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> study in 2000,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> the town centres were ranked by area thus (including North Lincolnshire and North East Lincolnshire areas):</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lincoln,_England" title="Lincoln, England">Lincoln</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grantham" title="Grantham">Grantham</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grimsby" title="Grimsby">Grimsby</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Boston,_Lincolnshire" title="Boston, Lincolnshire">Boston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe" title="Scunthorpe">Scunthorpe</a> (equal)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Spalding,_Lincolnshire" title="Spalding, Lincolnshire">Spalding</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stamford,_Lincolnshire" title="Stamford, Lincolnshire">Stamford</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Skegness" title="Skegness">Skegness</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Louth,_Lincolnshire" title="Louth, Lincolnshire">Louth</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sleaford" title="Sleaford">Sleaford</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gainsborough,_Lincolnshire" title="Gainsborough, Lincolnshire">Gainsborough</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brigg" title="Brigg">Brigg</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cleethorpes" title="Cleethorpes">Cleethorpes</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bourne,_Lincolnshire" title="Bourne, Lincolnshire">Bourne</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Horncastle,_Lincolnshire" title="Horncastle, Lincolnshire">Horncastle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mablethorpe" title="Mablethorpe">Mablethorpe</a> (equal)</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_services">Public services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Public services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Lincolnshire" title="Education in Lincolnshire">Education in Lincolnshire</a></div>
<p>Lincolnshire is one of the few counties within the UK that still uses the <a href="/wiki/11-plus" class="mw-redirect" title="11-plus">11-plus</a> to decide who may attend <a href="/wiki/Grammar_schools_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammar schools in the United Kingdom">grammar school</a>. As a result, many towns in Lincolnshire have both a grammar school and a <a href="/wiki/Secondary_modern_school" title="Secondary modern school">secondary modern school</a>. Lincolnshire's rural character means that some larger villages also have primary schools and are served by buses to nearby high schools.</p>
<p>Lincoln itself, however, is primarily non-selective, as is the area within a radius of about seven miles. Within this area, almost all children attend <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_school" title="Comprehensive school">comprehensive schools</a>, though it is still possible to opt into the 11-plus system. This gives rise to the unusual result that those who pass the Eleven plus can attend a Grammar School outside the Lincoln Comprehensive area, but those who do not pass still attend a (partly non-selective) Comprehensive school.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Lincolnshire" title="Transport in Lincolnshire">Transport in Lincolnshire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Humber_Bridge_Sunset_Wideshot.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Humber_Bridge_Sunset_Wideshot.jpg/220px-Humber_Bridge_Sunset_Wideshot.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Humber_Bridge_Sunset_Wideshot.jpg/330px-Humber_Bridge_Sunset_Wideshot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Humber_Bridge_Sunset_Wideshot.jpg/440px-Humber_Bridge_Sunset_Wideshot.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Humber_Bridge_Sunset_Wideshot.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Humber_Bridge" title="Humber Bridge">Humber Bridge</a> connecting North Lincolnshire to the <a href="/wiki/East_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="East Riding of Yorkshire">East Riding of Yorkshire</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Being on the economic periphery of England, Lincolnshire's transport links are poorly developed compared with many other parts of the United Kingdom. The road network within the county is dominated by <a href="/wiki/Single_carriageway" title="Single carriageway">single carriageway</a> <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_road_numbering_scheme" title="Great Britain road numbering scheme">A roads</a> and local roads (B roads) as opposed to <a href="/wiki/Controlled-access_highway" title="Controlled-access highway">motorways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dual_carriageways" class="mw-redirect" title="Dual carriageways">dual carriageways</a> – the administrative county of Lincolnshire is one of the few UK counties without a motorway, and until several years ago, it was said that there was only about 35&#160;km (22&#160;mi) of dual carriageway in the whole of Lincolnshire. The <a href="/wiki/M180_motorway" title="M180 motorway">M180 motorway</a> passes through North Lincolnshire, splitting into two dual-carriageway trunk roads to the <a href="/wiki/Humber_Bridge" title="Humber Bridge">Humber Bridge</a> and Grimsby, and the <a href="/wiki/A46_road" title="A46 road">A46</a> is now dual carriageway between <a href="/wiki/Newark-on-Trent" title="Newark-on-Trent">Newark-on-Trent</a> and Lincoln.</p>
<p>The low population density of the county means that the number of railway stations and train services is very low considering the county's large area. Many of the county's railway stations were permanently closed following the <a href="/wiki/Beeching_Axe" class="mw-redirect" title="Beeching Axe">Beeching Report</a> of 1963. The most notable reopening has been the line and two stations between Lincoln and <a href="/wiki/Sleaford" title="Sleaford">Sleaford</a>, which reopened within months of the Beeching closure. Most other closed lines within the county were long ago lifted and much of the trackbed has returned to agricultural use.</p>
<p>A daily through train service operated between <a href="/wiki/Cleethorpes" title="Cleethorpes">Cleethorpes</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King's Cross railway station">London King's Cross</a> via <a href="/wiki/Grimsby" title="Grimsby">Grimsby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Market_Rasen" title="Market Rasen">Market Rasen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Central_railway_station" title="Lincoln Central railway station">Lincoln Central</a> until the late 1980s. The Humberlincs Executive, as the service was known, was operated by a <a href="/wiki/InterCity_125" title="InterCity 125">HST125</a> unit, but was discontinued following the electrification of the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a>. Passengers now have to change trains at <a href="/wiki/Newark_North_Gate_railway_station" title="Newark North Gate railway station">Newark</a> when travelling to and from London. However, the East Coast Main Line passes through the county and one can catch direct trains to London.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincsroad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Lincsroad.jpg/220px-Lincsroad.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Lincsroad.jpg/330px-Lincsroad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Lincsroad.jpg/440px-Lincsroad.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincsroad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A rural road in Lincolnshire</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gosberton_Fen.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Gosberton_Fen.JPG/220px-Gosberton_Fen.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Gosberton_Fen.JPG/330px-Gosberton_Fen.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Gosberton_Fen.JPG/440px-Gosberton_Fen.JPG 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="720" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gosberton_Fen.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The rural <a href="/wiki/B1397_road" class="mw-redirect" title="B1397 road">B1397</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gosberton" title="Gosberton">Gosberton Fen</a> heading out towards the <a href="/wiki/Bourne,_Lincolnshire" title="Bourne, Lincolnshire">Bourne</a> area</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A proposed 2 hourly service promised by <a href="/wiki/National_Express_East_Coast" title="National Express East Coast">National Express East Coast</a> (who lost the franchise on 13 November 2009) between Lincoln and King's Cross has yet to start running, though was promised to start running by 2010.</p>
<p>Most rail services are currently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> provided by <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Trains" title="East Midlands Trains">East Midlands Trains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a>. <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Trains_East_Coast" title="Virgin Trains East Coast">Virgin Trains East Coast</a> and <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> have services which pass through the county, with Virgin Trains East Coast frequently passing and stopping at Grantham on the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a> and a daily return train to <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Central_railway_station" title="Lincoln Central railway station">Lincoln</a> which is at the end of the branch line, while CrossCountry trains stop at Stamford on their way between <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stansted_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Stansted Airport">Stansted Airport</a>. Stations along the Humber are served by <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> services between <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a> and Cleethorpes. One of the most infrequent services in the UK is in Lincolnshire: the Sheffield-<a href="/wiki/Gainsborough_Central" class="mw-redirect" title="Gainsborough Central">Gainsborough Central</a>-Cleethorpes line has passenger trains only on a Saturday, with three trains in both directions. This line is, however, used for freight.</p>
<p>On 22 May 2011 <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_(train_operating_company)" title="East Coast (train operating company)">East Coast</a> started a Lincoln-London service. One train travels both ways each day, and there is a northbound service on a Sunday. East Midlands Trains also run a daily (Mon-Sat) service each way between Lincoln and <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">London St Pancras</a>, though this is a stopping service which takes around 3 hours via Nottingham, compared to Virgin Trains East Coast's service to London King's Cross which takes around 1h 50 minutes.</p>
<p>The only airport in Lincolnshire is <a href="/wiki/Humberside_Airport" title="Humberside Airport">Humberside Airport</a>, near Brigg. While small, it serves all of Lincolnshire. <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_Sheffield_Airport" title="Doncaster Sheffield Airport">Doncaster Sheffield Airport</a> near <a href="/wiki/Doncaster" title="Doncaster">Doncaster</a> is within travelling distance of much of Lincolnshire and provide a wider range of flights.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The county's biggest bus companies are <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_Grimsby-Cleethorpes" title="Stagecoach Grimsby-Cleethorpes">Stagecoach Grimsby-Cleethorpes</a> (formerly Grimsby-Cleethorpes Transport) and <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_in_Lincolnshire" title="Stagecoach in Lincolnshire">Stagecoach in Lincolnshire</a>, (formerly Lincolnshire Road Car). There are several smaller bus companies, including Brylaine of Boston, <a href="/wiki/Delaine" class="mw-redirect" title="Delaine">Delaine of Bourne</a> and Hornsby's of Scunthorpe'<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Sustrans" title="Sustrans">Sustrans</a> cycle route runs from Lincoln to Boston in the south of the county.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">Health care</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Health care">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Lincolnshire_Hospitals_NHS_Trust" title="United Lincolnshire Hospitals NHS Trust">United Lincolnshire Hospitals NHS Trust</a><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> is one of the largest trusts in the country, employing almost 4,000 staff and with an annual budget of over £200&#160;million. The north of the county is served by the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nlg.nhs.uk/">Northern Lincolnshire and Goole Hospital NHS Foundation Trust</a>.</p>
<p>Lincolnshire shares the problems of elsewhere in the country when it comes to finding an NHS dentist, with waiting lists of eight months not uncommon.</p>
<p>Some of the larger hospitals in the county include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Diana_Princess_of_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="Diana Princess of Wales">Diana Princess of Wales</a> Hospital, Grimsby</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe_General_Hospital" title="Scunthorpe General Hospital">Scunthorpe General Hospital</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pilgrim_Hospital" title="Pilgrim Hospital">Boston Pilgrim Hospital</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lincoln_County_Hospital" title="Lincoln County Hospital">Lincoln County Hospital</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Since April 1994, Lincolnshire has had an Air <a href="/wiki/Air_ambulances_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Air ambulances in the United Kingdom">Ambulance service</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The air ambulance is stationed at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Waddington" title="RAF Waddington">RAF Waddington</a> near Lincoln and can reach emergencies in Lincolnshire within 25 minutes. An A&amp;E hospital is only 10 minutes away by helicopter from any accident in Lincolnshire.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drainage">Drainage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Drainage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Separately to the commercial water companies the low-lying parts of the county are drained by various <a href="/wiki/Internal_drainage_board" title="Internal drainage board">internal drainage boards</a>, such as the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.blacksluiceidb.gov.uk/">Black Sluice Internal Drainage Board</a>,<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://w4idb.co.uk/">Witham 4th District IDB</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.lmdb.co.uk/">Lindsey Marsh Drainage Board</a>, or the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.wellandidb.org.uk/">Welland and Deepings Internal Drainage Board</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lincolnshire is now the second fastest growing county in the UK with thousands of people moving there every year. Over the next two decades Lincolnshire is set to grow both in population and economy with the help of the Government’s Growth Points strategy. Lincolnshire has been awarded £13 million in funding to deliver sustainable development and intensive growth through sites of key regional significance. In essence, the target for Lincoln is 14,000 new homes and 12,000 new jobs by 2026 whilst the target for Grantham is an additional 3,200 homes by 2016 and at least 6,200 by 2026. This housing growth will be supported by the provision for 4,800 jobs by 2016.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Towns_and_villages">Towns and villages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Towns and villages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The non-metropolitan county of Lincolnshire has no major urban areas, apart from the areas in and around Lincoln, Grantham and <a href="/wiki/Boston,_Lincolnshire" title="Boston, Lincolnshire">Boston</a>. However, the <a href="/wiki/Skegness" title="Skegness">Skegness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ingoldmells" title="Ingoldmells">Ingoldmells</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chapel_St_Leonards" title="Chapel St Leonards">Chapel St Leonards</a> areas (and to a lesser extent the <a href="/wiki/Sutton-on-Sea" title="Sutton-on-Sea">Sutton-on-Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mablethorpe" title="Mablethorpe">Mablethorpe</a> areas) along the Lincolnshire coast are becoming increasingly urbanised, as people holiday at large caravan sites during the summer. These holidaymakers are not reflected in census or local population figures, though it is estimated that at the height of the summer months there are over 100,000 such residents in these coastal areas. This has an appreciable impact on the local infrastructure and amenities.</p>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincolnshire_UK_parish_map_(blank).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Lincolnshire_UK_parish_map_%28blank%29.svg/220px-Lincolnshire_UK_parish_map_%28blank%29.svg.png" width="220" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Lincolnshire_UK_parish_map_%28blank%29.svg/330px-Lincolnshire_UK_parish_map_%28blank%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Lincolnshire_UK_parish_map_%28blank%29.svg/440px-Lincolnshire_UK_parish_map_%28blank%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1086" data-file-height="1305" /></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coastal_tourism">Coastal tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Coastal tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>The majority of tourism in Lincolnshire relies on the coastal resorts and towns to the east of the <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_Wolds" title="Lincolnshire Wolds">Lincolnshire Wolds</a>. The county has some of the best-known seaside resorts in the United Kingdom, which are a major attraction to visitors from across England, especially the <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands" title="East Midlands">East Midlands</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a>. There are three main coastal resorts in Lincolnshire, and several smaller village resorts.</p>
<p>The main county seaside resort of <a href="/wiki/Skegness" title="Skegness">Skegness</a> with its famous <a href="/wiki/The_Jolly_Fisherman" title="The Jolly Fisherman">Jolly Fisherman</a> mascot and famous slogan "Skegness is so bracing", together with its neighbouring large village coastal resorts of <a href="/wiki/Ingoldmells" title="Ingoldmells">Ingoldmells</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chapel_St_Leonards" title="Chapel St Leonards">Chapel St Leonards</a>, provides the biggest concentration of resorts along the <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_Coast" class="mw-redirect" title="Lincolnshire Coast">Lincolnshire Coast</a>, with many large caravan and holiday sites. The resort offers many amusements, beaches, leisure activities and shops, as well as <a href="/wiki/Butlins_Skegness" title="Butlins Skegness">Butlins Skegness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fantasy_Island_(UK_amusement_park)" title="Fantasy Island (UK amusement park)">Fantasy Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Church_Farm_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Church Farm Museum">Church Farm Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natureland_Seal_Sanctuary" title="Natureland Seal Sanctuary">Natureland Seal Sanctuary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skegness_Stadium" title="Skegness Stadium">Skegness Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skegness_Pier#Pier" class="mw-redirect" title="Skegness Pier">Skegness Pier</a> and several well-known local golf courses. There are good road, bus and rail links to the rest of the county.</p>
<p>The second largest group of resorts along the coast is the small seaside town of <a href="/wiki/Mablethorpe" title="Mablethorpe">Mablethorpe</a>, famous for its golden sands, and the neighbouring village resorts of <a href="/wiki/Trusthorpe" title="Trusthorpe">Trusthorpe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sutton-on-Sea" title="Sutton-on-Sea">Sutton-on-Sea</a>. This area also offers leisure activities, and has large caravan and holiday sites. But the area is less developed, with fewer amusement arcades and nightclubs, and poorer road links to the rest of the county; but the area offers a more traditional seaside setting. The rail service to these towns was axed in the <a href="/wiki/Beeching_cuts" title="Beeching cuts">Beeching cuts</a>.</p>
<p>The third group of resorts includes the seaside town of <a href="/wiki/Cleethorpes" title="Cleethorpes">Cleethorpes</a> and the large village resort of <a href="/wiki/Humberston" title="Humberston">Humberston</a> within North East Lincolnshire. It has <a href="/wiki/Pleasure_Island_Family_Theme_Park" title="Pleasure Island Family Theme Park">Pleasure Island Family Theme Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cleethorpes_Coast_Light_Railway" title="Cleethorpes Coast Light Railway">Cleethorpes Coast Light Railway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cleethorpes_Pier" title="Cleethorpes Pier">Cleethorpes Pier</a> along with its local golf courses and caravan and holiday sites. Cleethorpes is well-served by road and rail; it is easily accessible from the <a href="/wiki/M180_motorway" title="M180 motorway">M180</a> and the <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> route to Manchester.</p>
<p>Nature is an attraction for many tourists: the south-east of the county is mainly fenland that attracts many species of birds, as do the nature reserves at <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Point" title="Gibraltar Point">Gibraltar Point</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saltfleetby" title="Saltfleetby">Saltfleetby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Theddlethorpe" title="Theddlethorpe">Theddlethorpe</a>. The reserve at <a href="/wiki/Donna_Nook" title="Donna Nook">Donna Nook</a> also has a native <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">seal</a> colony popular with nature lovers.</p>
<p>The market towns of the Lincolnshire Wolds (<a href="/wiki/Louth,_Lincolnshire" title="Louth, Lincolnshire">Louth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alford,_Lincolnshire" title="Alford, Lincolnshire">Alford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horncastle,_Lincolnshire" title="Horncastle, Lincolnshire">Horncastle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caistor" title="Caistor">Caistor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spilsby" title="Spilsby">Spilsby</a>) are also attractive, with several having historic links.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Cleanup" title="Wikipedia:Cleanup"><span title="Wikipedia:Cleanup">with what?</span></a></i>]</sup> The Wolds are quite popular for cycling and walking, with regular events such as the Lincolnshire Wolds Walking Festival.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincoln_Cathedral_in_Snow.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Lincoln_Cathedral_in_Snow.JPG/220px-Lincoln_Cathedral_in_Snow.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Lincoln_Cathedral_in_Snow.JPG/330px-Lincoln_Cathedral_in_Snow.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Lincoln_Cathedral_in_Snow.JPG/440px-Lincoln_Cathedral_in_Snow.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mobile_Library_(geograph_3691202).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Mobile_Library_%28geograph_3691202%29.jpg/220px-Mobile_Library_%28geograph_3691202%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Mobile_Library_%28geograph_3691202%29.jpg/330px-Mobile_Library_%28geograph_3691202%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Mobile_Library_%28geograph_3691202%29.jpg/440px-Mobile_Library_%28geograph_3691202%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3264" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mobile_Library_(geograph_3691202).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lincolnshire mobile library at <a href="/wiki/Pode_Hole" title="Pode Hole">Pode Hole</a>. <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_County_Council" title="Lincolnshire County Council">Lincolnshire County Council</a> operate five routes, covering small villages in this large, sparse, county. Each location is visited once a month.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Lincolnshire is a rural area where the pace of life is generally much slower than in much of the United Kingdom. Sunday is still largely a day of rest, with only shops in Lincoln, larger market towns, and resorts and industrial towns of the North Sea coast generally remaining open. Some towns and villages in the county still observe half-day closing on Thursdays. Due to the large distances between the towns, many villages have remained very self-contained, with many still having shops, pubs, local halls and local chapels and churches, offering a variety of social activities for residents. Fishing (in the extensive river and drainage system in the fens) and shooting are popular activities. A lot of the culture in Lincoln itself is based upon its history. <a href="/wiki/The_Collection_(Lincolnshire)" title="The Collection (Lincolnshire)">The Collection</a> is an archaeological museum and art galley in Lincoln. Lincoln Cathedral also plays a large part in Lincoln's culture, playing host to many events throughout the year, from concert recitals to indoor food markets.</p>
<p>A Lincolnshire tradition was that front doors were used for only three things: a new baby, a bride, and a coffin.<sup id="cite_ref-Sayings_and_Traditions_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sayings_and_Traditions-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: People">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lincolnshire is relatively unusual in the composition of its population, being one of the least ethnically diverse counties of the United Kingdom (98.5% of the population describe themselves as "white"). Over recent years inward migration by people from ethnic minority communities has increased (particularly to population centres such as Lincoln and Boston) but the absolute number of non-white Lincolnshire residents remains very low.</p>
<p>Recently, the county has also witnessed a growing trend towards immigration of retired people from other parts of the United Kingdom, particularly those from the southern counties of England attracted by the generally lower property prices and the slower and more relaxed pace of life. The relatively high proportion of elderly and retired people is reflected in many of the services, activities and events. Sleaford is considered one of the fastest-growing towns in the <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands" title="East Midlands">East Midlands</a>, with many professional people moving there to benefit from the (relatively) low house prices and crime rate, and the <a href="/wiki/Grammar_schools_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammar schools in the United Kingdom">selective education</a>.</p>
<p>Those born in Lincolnshire are sometimes given the nickname of <a href="/wiki/Yellowbelly_(Lincolnshire)" title="Yellowbelly (Lincolnshire)">Yellowbellies</a> (often spelt "Yeller Bellies", to reflect the pronunciation of the phrase by the typical Lincolnshire farmer). The origin of this term is debated, but is most commonly believed to derive from the uniform of the <a href="/wiki/10th_Regiment_of_Foot" class="mw-redirect" title="10th Regiment of Foot">10th Regiment of Foot</a> (later the <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_Regiment" class="mw-redirect" title="Lincolnshire Regiment">Lincolnshire Regiment</a>) which featured yellow facings. For this reason, the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> of Lincolnshire County Council is supported by two officers of the regiment.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
