</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_dialect">Local dialect</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Local dialect">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In common with most other <a href="/wiki/English_English#Northern_England" class="mw-redirect" title="English English">Northern</a> and <a href="/wiki/English_English#Midlands" class="mw-redirect" title="English English">Midlands dialects</a> in England, "flat" <i>a</i> is preferred, i.e. <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="/θ/: 'th' in 'thigh'">θ</span></span>/</a></span></span> over <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="/θ/: 'th' in 'thigh'">θ</span></span>/</a></span></span>, and also traditionally in words like <b>water</b>, pronounced <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ˈwætər/</span> <i>watter</i> (though such a pronunciation is rarely heard nowadays). Similarly, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ʌ/</span> is usually replaced by <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ʊ/</span>. Features rather more confined to Lincolnshire include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Elaboration of <a href="/wiki/Received_Pronunciation" title="Received Pronunciation">standard English</a> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/eɪ/</span> or <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/iː/</span> into a complex <a href="/wiki/Triphthong" title="Triphthong">triphthong</a> approximating, and often <a href="/wiki/Transcription_(linguistics)" title="Transcription (linguistics)">transcribed</a> <i>-air-</i> or <i>-yair-</i>. For example: "<b>mate</b>" <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[m(j)ɛːət]</span>; "<b>beast</b>" <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[b(j)ɛːəst]</span>; "<b>tates</b>" (potatoes) <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[t(j)ɛːəts]</span>.</li>
<li>An equivalent elaboration of standard English <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/oʊ/</span> – commonly <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[oː]</span> in <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">Northern England</a> – into <i>-ooa-</i>. For example, "<b>boat</b>" <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[bʊːət]</span>.</li>
<li>Insertion of an extra <a href="/wiki/Schwa" title="Schwa">schwa</a> into the standard English <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthong</a> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/aʊ/</span>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vocabulary" title="Vocabulary">Vocabulary</a>: "<b>duck</b>" as a term of endearment or informal address, "<b>mardy</b>" meaning upset or angry, "<b>mowt</b>" (pronounced like mout) for <i>might</i>,"<b>while</b>" as a substitute for standard English "until", "<b>frit</b>" meaning frightened, "<b>grufty</b>" meaning dirty or disgusting, and the inimitable <a href="/wiki/Salutation_(greeting)" class="mw-redirect" title="Salutation (greeting)">salutation</a> "<b>now then!?</b>" (hello), sometimes written <i>nairn</i> to reflect pronunciation.</li>
<li>In the north east of the county, around Grimsby and Immingham, the <a href="/wiki/Phonological_history_of_English_vowels" title="Phonological history of English vowels">nurse-square merger</a> can be heard, as is also the case along the east coast of Yorkshire and also in Liverpool. Words that take <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɜː/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Received_pronunciation" class="mw-redirect" title="Received pronunciation">RP</a> take <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɛː/</span> in these areas.</li>
</ul>
<p>Lincolnshire has its own dialect "champion", a farmer from the village of <a href="/wiki/Minting" title="Minting">Minting</a> called Farmer Wink (real name Robert Carlton), who has produced videos about rural life, narrated in his broad Lincolnshire accent, and has a regular slot on <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Lincolnshire" title="BBC Radio Lincolnshire">BBC Radio Lincolnshire</a>. A resident of <a href="/wiki/Woodhall_Spa" title="Woodhall Spa">Woodhall Spa</a> has published a dictionary of words once prevalent in parts of the county.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lincolnshire was historically associated with the <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_bagpipe" class="mw-redirect" title="Lincolnshire bagpipe">Lincolnshire bagpipe</a>, an instrument derided as a coarse and unpleasant instrument in contemporary literature, but noted as very popular in the county. The last player, <a href="/wiki/John_Hunsley" title="John Hunsley">John Hunsley</a> of Middle Manton,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> died in 1851,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> and since then the instrument has been extinct.</p>
<p>In 1937, <a href="/wiki/Percy_Grainger" title="Percy Grainger">Percy Grainger</a> wrote his <i><a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_Posy" title="Lincolnshire Posy">Lincolnshire Posy</a></i> for wind band. The piece is a compilation of folk songs "musical wildflowers" collected by the composer in and around the county of Lincolnshire.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Lincolnshire_Poacher" title="The Lincolnshire Poacher">The Lincolnshire Poacher</a></i> is a traditional <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English</a> <a href="/wiki/Folk_song" class="mw-redirect" title="Folk song">folk song</a> associated with the county of Lincolnshire, and deals with the joys of <a href="/wiki/Poaching" title="Poaching">poaching</a>. It is considered to be the unofficial county anthem of Lincolnshire.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Food">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincolnshire_sausages_and_onions.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Lincolnshire_sausages_and_onions.jpg/200px-Lincolnshire_sausages_and_onions.jpg" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Lincolnshire_sausages_and_onions.jpg/300px-Lincolnshire_sausages_and_onions.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Lincolnshire_sausages_and_onions.jpg/400px-Lincolnshire_sausages_and_onions.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincolnshire_sausages_and_onions.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_sausages" class="mw-redirect" title="Lincolnshire sausages">Lincolnshire sausages</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Lincolnshire has a number of local dishes:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stuffed_chine" title="Stuffed chine">Stuffed chine</a> – this is salted neck-chine of a pig taken from between the shoulder blades, salted for up to ten months and stuffed with <a href="/wiki/Parsley" title="Parsley">parsley</a> (other ingredients are normally kept secret), and served cold.<sup id="cite_ref-Ports1937_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ports1937-19">[19]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Haslet" title="Haslet">Haslet</a> – a type of pork loaf, also flavoured with sage (pronounced HAYSS-let or AYSS-let in Lincolnshire but HAZ-let in many other parts of the country).<sup id="cite_ref-Ports1937_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ports1937-19">[19]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_sausage" title="Lincolnshire sausage">Lincolnshire sausages</a> – most butchers in Lincolnshire have their own secret recipe for these and a competition is held each year to judge the best sausages in the county. Traditional Lincolnshire sausages are made entirely from minced pork, stale bread crumb (<a href="/wiki/Rusk" title="Rusk">rusk</a> is used nowadays) pepper, sage and salt. The skins should be natural casings which are made from the intestines of either sheep or pig.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pork_pie" title="Pork pie">Pork pies</a> – the same pork butchers will take a pride in their unique recipe for pork pies.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Giblets" title="Giblets">Giblet</a> pie.<sup id="cite_ref-Ports1937_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ports1937-19">[19]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lamb_and_mutton" title="Lamb and mutton">Mutton</a> stuffed with <a href="/wiki/Oyster" title="Oyster">oysters</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ports1937_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ports1937-19">[19]</a></sup></li>
<li>Plum bread – as with <a href="/wiki/Christmas_pudding" title="Christmas pudding">plum pudding</a>, plum refers to <a href="/wiki/Dried_fruit" title="Dried fruit">dried fruit</a>, namely currants, raisins and sultanas, sometimes soaked in tea.</li>
<li>Grantham Gingerbread – a hard white ginger biscuit.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_Poacher_cheese" title="Lincolnshire Poacher cheese">Lincolnshire Poacher cheese</a> – a cheddar-style cheese produced in <a href="/wiki/Alford,_Lincolnshire" title="Alford, Lincolnshire">Alford</a>. Lincolnshire Poacher has won numerous awards over the years including Supreme Champion at the 1996/7 British Cheese Awards and Best British Cheese at the World Cheese awards in 2001/2.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Batemans_Brewery" title="Batemans Brewery">Batemans</a> ales – a beer brewed in <a href="/wiki/Wainfleet,_Lincolnshire" title="Wainfleet, Lincolnshire">Wainfleet</a> and served in many pubs in the county and further afield.</li>
<li>There are several small breweries.</li>
<li>Grimsby is renowned for its fishing industry, and historically <i>Grimsby Fish</i> has carried a premium price. Since the decline of the fishing industry following entry to the European Economic Community in the 1970s this is no longer the case, with the majority of fish sold at the town's fish market being brought overland from other ports. However, <i>Grimsby Fish</i> is still a recognised <i>product</i>, one associated with a particular area that specialises in and has expertise in a particular trade (cf <i>Sheffield steel</i>). In 2009 <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Grimsby_smoked_fish" title="Traditional Grimsby smoked fish">smoked fish</a> from the town was granted <a href="/wiki/Protected_Geographical_Indication" class="mw-redirect" title="Protected Geographical Indication">Protected Geographical Indication</a> by the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, reflecting the unique smoking methods used by certain local fish companies.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Craft Chocolatiers can be found throughout<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> the county, such as Hansens<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> in Folkingham.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> In 2013 Redstar Chocolate's <i>Duffy's Venezuela Ocumare Milk</i> won a Gold medal as best bean-to-bar.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The factory is in Cleethorpes.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Every year the Lincolnshire Agricultural Society, founded in 1869, stages the Lincolnshire Agricultural Show.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> It is held on the Wednesday and Thursday of the last whole week of June at its showground at <a href="/wiki/Grange_de_Lings" title="Grange de Lings">Grange de Lings</a>, a few miles north of Lincoln on the <a href="/wiki/A15_road_(Great_Britain)" class="mw-redirect" title="A15 road (Great Britain)">A15</a>. The show was first held here in 1958. First held around the year 1884, it is one of the largest agricultural shows in the country, and is attended by around 100,000 people over its two days. The showground is in regular use throughout the year for a wide range of other events and functions.</p>
<p>Smaller local agricultural shows, such as the <a href="/wiki/Heckington" title="Heckington">Heckington</a> Show<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> can still be found. <a href="/wiki/Corby_Glen" title="Corby Glen">Corby Glen</a> sheep fair<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> has been held since 1238.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Red_Arrows_03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Red_Arrows_03.jpg/220px-Red_Arrows_03.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Red_Arrows_03.jpg/330px-Red_Arrows_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Red_Arrows_03.jpg/440px-Red_Arrows_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Red_Arrows_03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Red_Arrows" title="Red Arrows">Red Arrows</a>, based at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Scampton" title="RAF Scampton">RAF Scampton</a> near Lincoln<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> are a popular attraction at the Waddington Air Show</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Each year <a href="/wiki/RAF_Waddington" title="RAF Waddington">RAF Waddington</a> is the home to the RAF International Waddington Air Show. The two-day event attracts around 150,000 people and usually takes place during the first weekend of July. Since its inception over 35 countries have participated, with aircraft from around the globe attending the Lincolnshire Base. Beginning 2017, the event will be held at nearby RAF Scampton.</p>
<p>On the Monday before Easter, an unusual auction takes place in <a href="/wiki/Bourne,_Lincolnshire" title="Bourne, Lincolnshire">Bourne</a> to let the grazing rights of the Whitebread Meadow.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Bidding takes place while two boys race toward the Queen's Bridge in Eastgate, the end of which dash is equivalent to the falling of the gavel. The whole affair dates back to the 1742 will of William Clay.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Haxey_Hood" title="Haxey Hood">Haxey Hood</a> village competition takes place every January, as it has for over 700 years.</p>
<p>Stamford's Mid-Lent fair sees showmen converge on the town the week after <a href="/wiki/Mothering_Sunday" title="Mothering Sunday">Mothering Sunday</a>, with rides and sideshows filling Broad Street, the Sheepmarket and the Meadows for a week. Stalls selling Grantham gingerbread and nougat are a traditional feature. The following week sees them in Grantham, on the way North for the Summer. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.rogertuby.co.uk/">Roger Tuby</a> brings a small funfair to Bourne and then to Spalding in Spring and returns in Autumn at the end of the season.</p>
<p>The villages of <a href="/wiki/Tetford" title="Tetford">Tetford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salmonby" title="Salmonby">Salmonby</a> hold an annual Scarecrow Festival in May every year.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Belchford" title="Belchford">Belchford</a> Downhill Challenge which is held every two years: soapbox racers race down the hill at up to 30&#160;km/h. The turnout has been up to 1,000.</p>
<p>In recent years <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Christmas_Market" title="Lincoln Christmas Market">Lincoln Christmas Market</a>, a street market throughout historic area of the city, has been held at the start of December. Around the same time Christmas lights are turned on in Bourne, Sleaford, Skegness, and other towns.</p>
<p>Throughout the summer the <a href="/wiki/Stamford_Shakespeare_Company" title="Stamford Shakespeare Company">Stamford Shakespeare Company</a><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> presents the Bard's plays in the open-air theatre at <a href="/wiki/Tolethorpe_Hall" title="Tolethorpe Hall">Tolethorpe Hall</a>, which is actually in <a href="/wiki/Rutland" title="Rutland">Rutland</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Spalding,_Lincolnshire" title="Spalding, Lincolnshire">Spalding</a> Flower Parade is held in late spring every year. Colourful floats decorated with tulip heads compete for a cup. The tradition was started in 1959 and draws coach tours from across Britain.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincoln_Gold_Postbox.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Lincoln_Gold_Postbox.jpg/220px-Lincoln_Gold_Postbox.jpg" width="220" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Lincoln_Gold_Postbox.jpg/330px-Lincoln_Gold_Postbox.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Lincoln_Gold_Postbox.jpg/440px-Lincoln_Gold_Postbox.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1635" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincoln_Gold_Postbox.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Gold Victorian-style Penfold post box in Lincoln painted in recognition of Paralympian <a href="/wiki/Sophie_Wells" title="Sophie Wells">Sophie Wells</a> who won the gold medal in the team Equestrian event at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Paralympic_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="2012 Paralympic Games">2012 Paralympic Games</a> in London. It is the only post box painted gold within the county</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The main sports played in the county are <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>. Lincolnshire does not have a high sporting profile, mainly due to the lack of facilities and high-profile football teams. Probably the most well known sporting venues in Lincolnshire are <a href="/wiki/Cadwell_Park" title="Cadwell Park">Cadwell Park</a> near Louth, where a round of the British Motorbike Championship is held on the last Monday of August every year and the racecourse at <a href="/wiki/Market_Rasen" title="Market Rasen">Market Rasen</a></p>
<ul>
<li>Three teams from Lincolnshire play in the <a href="/wiki/Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League">Football League</a>: <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe_United_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Scunthorpe United FC">Scunthorpe United</a> play in <a href="/wiki/Football_League_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League One">Football League One</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_City_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Lincoln City FC">Lincoln City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grimsby_Town_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Grimsby Town FC">Grimsby Town</a> play in <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Two" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Two">Football League Two</a>. In non-league football <a href="/wiki/Boston_United_F.C." title="Boston United F.C.">Boston United</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gainsborough_Trinity_F.C." title="Gainsborough Trinity F.C.">Gainsborough Trinity</a> play in the <a href="/wiki/Football_Conference_North" class="mw-redirect" title="Football Conference North">Football Conference North</a>.</li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Lincolnshire County Cricket Club">Lincolnshire</a> are a minor county and play in the <a href="/wiki/Minor_Counties_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor Counties Championship">Minor Counties Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">hockey</a> <a href="/wiki/Lindum_Hockey_Club" title="Lindum Hockey Club">Lindum Hockey Club</a> play in the North of Lincoln.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe_Rugby_Club" title="Scunthorpe Rugby Club">Scunthorpe Rugby Club</a> are the most notable <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> team from Lincolnshire, and will play in the fifth level of the English league system in the 2017-18 season. Other notable teams include Market Rasen and Louth RUFC, Lincoln RFC, and <a href="/wiki/Boston_Rugby_Club" title="Boston Rugby Club">Boston Rugby Club</a>.</li>
<li>Lincolnshire is home to one racecourse, at <a href="/wiki/Market_Rasen_Racecourse" title="Market Rasen Racecourse">Market Rasen</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cadwell_Park" title="Cadwell Park">Cadwell Park</a> is the only motor-racing course in Lincolnshire. There is a speedway track in Scunthorpe, home of the <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe_Scorpions" title="Scunthorpe Scorpions">Scunthorpe Scorpions</a>, and stock-car racing at a stadium at Orby, near <a href="/wiki/Skegness" title="Skegness">Skegness</a>.</li>
<li>Lincolnshire is home to the UK <a href="/wiki/Roller_derby" title="Roller derby">roller derby</a> team the Lincolnshire Bombers Roller Girls, who are sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Mot%C3%B6rhead" title="Motörhead">Motörhead</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincolnshire_flag.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lincolnshire_flag.svg/220px-Lincolnshire_flag.svg.png" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lincolnshire_flag.svg/330px-Lincolnshire_flag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lincolnshire_flag.svg/440px-Lincolnshire_flag.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="540" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Lincoln_Imp_-_geograph.org.uk_-_356041.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/The_Lincoln_Imp_-_geograph.org.uk_-_356041.jpg/220px-The_Lincoln_Imp_-_geograph.org.uk_-_356041.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/The_Lincoln_Imp_-_geograph.org.uk_-_356041.jpg/330px-The_Lincoln_Imp_-_geograph.org.uk_-_356041.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/The_Lincoln_Imp_-_geograph.org.uk_-_356041.jpg/440px-The_Lincoln_Imp_-_geograph.org.uk_-_356041.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Lincoln_Imp_-_geograph.org.uk_-_356041.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Imp" title="Lincoln Imp">Lincoln Imp</a> high above the choir on the southern side of Lincoln Cathedral</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The unofficial anthem of the county is the traditional folk song, "<a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_Poacher_(folk_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lincolnshire Poacher (folk song)">The Lincolnshire Poacher</a>", which dates from around 1776. A version of the song was the theme for <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Lincolnshire" title="BBC Radio Lincolnshire">BBC Radio Lincolnshire</a> for many years.</p>
<p>According to a 2002 marketing campaign by the charity <a href="/wiki/Plantlife" title="Plantlife">Plantlife</a>, the <a href="/wiki/County_flower" class="mw-redirect" title="County flower">county flower</a> of Lincolnshire is the <a href="/wiki/Common_Dog-violet" class="mw-redirect" title="Common Dog-violet">Common Dog-violet</a>.</p>
<p>In August 2005, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Lincolnshire" title="BBC Radio Lincolnshire">BBC Radio Lincolnshire</a> and <i>Lincolnshire Life</i> magazine launched a vote for a flag to represent the county. Six competing designs were voted upon by locals. The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Lincolnshire" title="Flag of Lincolnshire">winning submission</a> was unveiled in October 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Lincoln has its own flag – St George's flag with a Fleur-de-Lys.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Imp" title="Lincoln Imp">Lincoln Imp</a> has symbolised cathedral, city, and county for many years.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In 2006 it was replaced as the brand of Lincolnshire County Council by the stylised version seen on the header here <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.lincolnshire.gov.uk/">[2]</a> which has lost even the unique pose of the carving.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Press">Press</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Press">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The county is home to one daily newspaper, the <i><a href="/wiki/Grimsby_Telegraph" title="Grimsby Telegraph">Grimsby Telegraph</a></i> which as the name suggests, is published in the town and whose circulation area ostensibly covers North East Lincolnshire, although it reaches as far south as Louth and Alford and as west as <a href="/wiki/Brigg" title="Brigg">Brigg</a>.</p>
<p>There are two further weekly papers which used to be published daily until 2011; the <i><a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_Echo" title="Lincolnshire Echo">Lincolnshire Echo</a></i> is published weekly from Lincoln and covers the majority of the county reaching as far north as Louth, and the <i><a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe_Telegraph" title="Scunthorpe Telegraph">Scunthorpe Telegraph</a></i> which covers northern Lincolnshire. All three are ultimately owned by the <a href="/wiki/Daily_Mail_and_General_Trust" title="Daily Mail and General Trust">Daily Mail and General Trust</a>.</p>
<p>There are also a number of weekly papers serving individual towns published in the county by <a href="/wiki/Johnston_Press" title="Johnston Press">Johnston Press</a>. One of these, the <i><a href="/wiki/Stamford_Mercury" title="Stamford Mercury">Stamford Mercury</a></i> claims to be Britain's oldest newspaper, although it is now a typical local weekly and no longer covers stories from the whole East Midlands as the archived copies did.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>With the exception of a small area to the south-west of the county,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Lincolnshire is served from the <a href="/wiki/Belmont_transmitting_station" title="Belmont transmitting station">Belmont transmitter</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> receiving programmes from <a href="/wiki/ITV_Yorkshire" title="ITV Yorkshire">ITV Yorkshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/BBC_One" title="BBC One">BBC One</a> <a href="/wiki/BBC_Yorkshire_and_Lincolnshire" title="BBC Yorkshire and Lincolnshire">Yorkshire and Lincolnshire</a> regions.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> has, since 2003, provided the area with its twelfth regional service: <a href="/wiki/BBC_Yorkshire_and_Lincolnshire" title="BBC Yorkshire and Lincolnshire">BBC Yorkshire and Lincolnshire</a>, carrying a local "<a href="/wiki/BBC_Look_North_(East_Yorkshire_and_Lincolnshire)" title="BBC Look North (East Yorkshire and Lincolnshire)">Look North</a>" news programme from the main studio in <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Hull</a>, with input from other studios in Lincoln and Grimsby.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/ITV_Yorkshire" title="ITV Yorkshire">ITV Yorkshire</a> provides coverage through its evening news programme "<a href="/wiki/Calendar_(News)" class="mw-redirect" title="Calendar (News)">Calendar</a>". Until late 2008 the station provided a separate edition for the Belmont transmitter (although it was still broadcast from Leeds). From January 2009 the area is now covered by a programme that covers the entire ITV Yorkshire region.</p>
<p>From 1959 to July 1974 <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> programmes were provided by <a href="/wiki/Anglia_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglia Television">Anglia Television</a> (although some coverage could be received from the <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Granada_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Granada Television">Granada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Associated_British_Corporation" title="Associated British Corporation">ABC Weekend</a>). Based in <a href="/wiki/Norwich" title="Norwich">Norwich</a> the company had news offices in Grimsby.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Following a transmitter change ITV services were provided by <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Yorkshire Television">Yorkshire Television</a>. This company kept open the offices in Grimsby and opened further facilities in Lincoln, although both of these closed in the mid-1990s.</p>
<p>South-West Lincolnshire receives <a href="/wiki/BBC_East_Midlands" title="BBC East Midlands">BBC East Midlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/ITV_Central" title="ITV Central">ITV Central</a> which are broadcast from the Waltham on The Wolds Transmitting Station. Although subject to <a href="/wiki/Co-channel_interference" title="Co-channel interference">co-channel interference</a> from the Waltham transmitter, a small number of households in the southern tip of the county<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> are able to receive regional programming from <a href="/wiki/BBC_East" title="BBC East">BBC East</a> and <a href="/wiki/ITV_Anglia" title="ITV Anglia">ITV Anglia</a>.</p>
<p>Many villages just west of the <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Cliff" title="Lincoln Cliff">Lincoln Edge</a> cannot get a signal from Belmont due to <a href="/wiki/Fading" title="Fading">shadowing</a> and instead get their TV from <a href="/wiki/Emley_Moor_transmitting_station" title="Emley Moor transmitting station">Emley Moor</a> near Huddersfield.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The area is covered by several local radio stations including:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincoln_City_Radio&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lincoln City Radio (page does not exist)">Lincoln City Radio</a> The only radio station dedicated to the over-50's in the City of Lincoln and the surrounding villages.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BBC_Lincolnshire" class="mw-redirect" title="BBC Lincolnshire">BBC Lincolnshire</a> Can be heard throughout historic Lincolnshire although its broadcast remit is the present county of Lincolnshire</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Humberside" title="BBC Radio Humberside">BBC Radio Humberside</a> The counties of northern Lincolnshire that were formerly known as South Humberside</li>
<li>Boundary Sound Newark (closed 2011)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Compass_FM" title="Compass FM">Compass FM</a> Grimsby, Cleethorpes and Immingham</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hereward_FM" class="mw-redirect" title="Hereward FM">Heart</a> Peterborough and South Lincolnshire</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lincs_FM" title="Lincs FM">Lincs FM</a> Historic Lincolnshire</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140114053400/http://www.gravityfm.net/">Gravity FM</a> Grantham</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Siren_FM" title="Siren FM">Siren FM</a> Lincoln</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.endeavourfm.co.uk/">Endeavour FM (formerly Stump Radio)</a> Boston</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.endeavourradio.co.uk/">Endeavour Radio</a> Boston</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tulip_Radio" title="Tulip Radio">Tulip Radio</a> Spalding and South Holland</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Viking_FM" title="Viking FM">Viking FM</a> Northern Lincolnshire and the <a href="/wiki/East_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="East Riding of Yorkshire">East Yorkshire</a>, formerly the constituent areas of <a href="/wiki/Humberside" title="Humberside">Humberside</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Landing_At_RAF_Coningsby_MOD_45155053.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Typhoon_Landing_At_RAF_Coningsby_MOD_45155053.jpg/220px-Typhoon_Landing_At_RAF_Coningsby_MOD_45155053.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Typhoon_Landing_At_RAF_Coningsby_MOD_45155053.jpg/330px-Typhoon_Landing_At_RAF_Coningsby_MOD_45155053.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Typhoon_Landing_At_RAF_Coningsby_MOD_45155053.jpg/440px-Typhoon_Landing_At_RAF_Coningsby_MOD_45155053.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3600" data-file-height="2354" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Landing_At_RAF_Coningsby_MOD_45155053.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Typhoon FGR.4 aircraft, based at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Coningsby" title="RAF Coningsby">RAF Coningsby</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a></div>
<p>Because of its flat geography and low population density, Lincolnshire is an ideal place for airfields, and the RAF built prolifically in the county, which has hosted nearly seventy separate bases. With the drawdown<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> of the RAF, most of these have closed, but the RAF retains a significant footprint. For more information on former bases, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_former_RAF_stations" class="mw-redirect" title="List of former RAF stations">List of former RAF stations</a>.</p>
<p>Lincolnshire is currently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (May 2017)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> home to a number of RAF stations, including two major front-line bases: <a href="/wiki/RAF_Coningsby" title="RAF Coningsby">RAF Coningsby</a>, which houses <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon" title="Eurofighter Typhoon">Typhoon jet fighters</a>; and <a href="/wiki/RAF_Waddington" title="RAF Waddington">RAF Waddington</a>, where most of the RAF's Intelligence, Surveillance, Target Acquisition and Reconnaissance aircraft are based. Other stations in Lincolnshire include <a href="/wiki/RAF_Cranwell" title="RAF Cranwell">RAF Cranwell</a>, home of all basic Officer training for the Royal Air Force; <a href="/wiki/RAF_Scampton" title="RAF Scampton">RAF Scampton</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Arrows" title="Red Arrows">Red Arrows</a>; <a href="/wiki/RAF_Barkston_Heath" title="RAF Barkston Heath">RAF Barkston Heath</a>, a training airfield; and minor bases such as <a href="/wiki/RAF_Kirton_in_Lindsey" title="RAF Kirton in Lindsey">RAF Kirton in Lindsey</a>, <a href="/wiki/RAF_Holbeach" title="RAF Holbeach">RAF Holbeach</a>, <a href="/wiki/RAF_Donna_Nook" title="RAF Donna Nook">RAF Donna Nook</a> and <a href="/wiki/RAF_Digby" title="RAF Digby">RAF Digby</a>.</p>
<p>The Army runs <a href="/wiki/Sobraon_Barracks" title="Sobraon Barracks">Sobraon Barracks</a>, home of 160 (Lincoln) Squadron, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Logistic_Corps" title="Royal Logistic Corps">Royal Logistic Corps</a> (RLC), as well as <a href="/wiki/Prince_William_of_Gloucester_Barracks" title="Prince William of Gloucester Barracks">Prince William of Gloucester Barracks</a>, Grantham, home to some of the RLC's Phase 2 training. In November 2016 the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">Ministry of Defence</a> announced that the Grantham site would close in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
